<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Kasseem Daoud Dean</b> (born September 13, 1978), known professionally as <b>Swizz Beatz</b>, is an American record producer, rapper, disc jockey (DJ) and songwriter. Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">the Bronx</a> borough of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, Dean initially embarked on his musical career as a <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">DJ</a>. At the age of 18, he started to gain recognition in the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> industry through his family's record label, <a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruff Ryders">Ruff Ryders</a>, as well as his friendship and work with <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_hip_hop" title="East Coast hip hop">Yonkers-based rapper</a> <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a>. Working with DMX as his producer, DJ and <a href="/wiki/Hype_man" title="Hype man">hype man</a>, helped Dean gain prominence as a high-profile personality in hip hop.
</p><p>Dean later found a protégé in Philadelphia-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Cassidy_(rapper)" title="Cassidy (rapper)">Cassidy</a>, whose success helped the launch of his own label imprint, <a href="/wiki/Full_Surface_Records" title="Full Surface Records">Full Surface</a>, in 2001. He went on to sign multiple artists to the label, including <a href="/wiki/Eve_(rapper)" title="Eve (rapper)">Eve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mashonda" title="Mashonda">Mashonda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bone_Thugs-n-Harmony" title="Bone Thugs-n-Harmony">Bone Thugs-n-Harmony</a>, among others. Dean went on to release two albums under the label; the first was a compilation, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz_Presents_G.H.E.T.T.O._Stories" title="Swizz Beatz Presents G.H.E.T.T.O. Stories">Swizz Beatz Presents G.H.E.T.T.O. Stories</a></i>, released in 2002, and later his debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/One_Man_Band_Man" title="One Man Band Man">One Man Band Man</a></i> in 2007. In November 2018, Dean released his second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Poison_(Swizz_Beatz_album)" title="Poison (Swizz Beatz album)">Poison</a></i>. Alongside fellow musician <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>, Dean is known for creating the popular webcast series <i><a href="/wiki/Verzuz" title="Verzuz">Verzuz</a></i> in 2020.
</p><p>Dean has produced several hit singles for a number of prominent artists across different music genres, such as <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>. With a career spanning over two decades, his catalog includes "<a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders%27_Anthem" title="Ruff Ryders&#39; Anthem">Ruff Ryders' Anthem</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Party_Up_(Up_in_Here)" title="Party Up (Up in Here)">Party Up (Up in Here)</a>" (DMX), "<a href="/wiki/Gotta_Man" title="Gotta Man">Gotta Man</a>" (Eve), "<a href="/wiki/Jigga_My_Nigga" title="Jigga My Nigga">Jigga My Nigga</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Girl%27s_Best_Friend" title="Girl&#39;s Best Friend">Girl's Best Friend</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>), "<a href="/wiki/Upgrade_U" title="Upgrade U">Upgrade U</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Check_on_It" title="Check on It">Check on It</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Ring_the_Alarm" title="Ring the Alarm">Ring the Alarm</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>), "<a href="/wiki/Good_Times_(Styles_P_song)" title="Good Times (Styles P song)">Good Times</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Styles_P" title="Styles P">Styles P</a>), "<a href="/wiki/Bring_Em_Out_(song)" title="Bring Em Out (song)">Bring 'Em Out</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Swing_Ya_Rag" title="Swing Ya Rag">Swing Ya Rag</a>" (<a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a>), "<a href="/wiki/Hotel_(Cassidy_song)" title="Hotel (Cassidy song)">Hotel</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_a_Hustla_(song)" title="I&#39;m a Hustla (song)">I'm a Hustla</a>" (Cassidy), "<a href="/wiki/Touch_It_(Busta_Rhymes_song)" title="Touch It (Busta Rhymes song)">Touch It</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a>), "<a href="/wiki/Ultralight_Beam" title="Ultralight Beam">Ultralight Beam</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>), <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz_production_discography" title="Swizz Beatz production discography">and more</a>.
</p><p>Dean was named the first "Producer in Residence" at <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> (NYU), for the 2010–11 academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/About.com" class="mw-redirect" title="About.com">About.com</a> ranked him number 27 on its list of the "Top 50 Greatest Hip-Hop Producers",<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Source (magazine)">The Source</a></i> included him on its list of the "20 greatest producers" in the magazine's 20-year history.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Fellow American rapper and producer <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> called Dean "the best rap producer of all time".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Aside from music, Dean has also added multiple entrepreneurial endeavors to his repertoire, including fashion design, art collecting, and <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board directing</a>. He has been a member of trustees at the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Museum" title="Brooklyn Museum">Brooklyn Museum</a> since 2015, and a creative director for the companies <a href="/wiki/Monster_Cable" title="Monster Cable">Monster Cable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Dean is married to American musician <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a>, with whom he has two children. The two were featured in their first cover shoot in 2018 for <i>Cultured Magazine</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1978.E2.80.932006:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1978–2006:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings">1978–2006: Early life and career beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1978–2006: Early life and career beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He spent much of his childhood raised by his mother in the North East <a href="/wiki/Bronx" class="mw-redirect" title="Bronx">Bronx</a>, where he first encountered <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a>. After obtaining the necessary equipment from his stepfather and uncles, he began <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">DJing</a> as a teenager and enjoyed a modicum of success. After relocating to <a href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlanta, Georgia">Atlanta, Georgia</a>, due to his repeated involvement in violent behavior at <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman_High_School_(New_York_City)" class="mw-redirect" title="Harry S. Truman High School (New York City)">Harry S. Truman High School</a>, he started to work for his uncles, Joaquin (Waah) and Darrin (Dee) Dean, who were co-CEOs of the <a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruff Ryders">Ruff Ryders</a> record label. In his early work, he generally chose not to <a href="/wiki/Sampling_(music)" title="Sampling (music)">sample</a>, instead using the <a href="/wiki/Korg_Trinity" title="Korg Trinity">Korg Trinity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Korg_Triton" title="Korg Triton">Triton</a> keyboards and seeking to accentuate the performance aspect of his music.
</p><p>With his uncles Waah &amp; Dee, as well as his aunt Chivon Dean, all involved with the Ruff Ryders record label, Swizz Beatz began to <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_production" title="Hip hop production">produce</a> tracks at age 16, and was signed to Ruff Ryders Productions as a producer and songwriter. A year later he sold his first beat to Ruff Ryders artist <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a>, which became his chart-topping single "<a href="/wiki/Ruff_Ryders%27_Anthem" title="Ruff Ryders&#39; Anthem">Ruff Ryders' Anthem</a>". The song was placed onto DMX's seminal 1998 debut album <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Dark_and_Hell_is_Hot" class="mw-redirect" title="It&#39;s Dark and Hell is Hot">It's Dark and Hell is Hot</a></i>. Dean then began producing major hip-hop songs released in 1998 such as "<a href="/wiki/Banned_from_T.V." title="Banned from T.V.">Banned from T.V.</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Noreaga" class="mw-redirect" title="Noreaga">Noreaga</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Money,_Cash,_Hoes" title="Money, Cash, Hoes">Money, Cash, Hoes</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and more. The following year, he produced most of the songs of the Ruff Ryders compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Ryde_or_Die_Vol._1" title="Ryde or Die Vol. 1">Ryde or Die Vol. 1</a></i>, as well as the bulk of <a href="/wiki/Eve_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eve (entertainer)">Eve</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Let_There_Be_Eve...Ruff_Ryders%27_First_Lady" title="Let There Be Eve...Ruff Ryders&#39; First Lady">debut album</a>. In 2001, in a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Clive_Davis" title="Clive Davis">Clive Davis</a>, Swizz Beatz established his own record label, <a href="/wiki/Full_Surface_Records" title="Full Surface Records">Full Surface Records</a>, which became a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/J_Records" title="J Records">J Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-umusicpub_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umusicpub-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The first artist signed was <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Cassidy_(rapper)" title="Cassidy (rapper)">Cassidy</a>.
</p><p>When Dean released his first compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz_Presents_G.H.E.T.T.O._Stories" title="Swizz Beatz Presents G.H.E.T.T.O. Stories">Swizz Beatz Presents G.H.E.T.T.O. Stories</a></i>, in 2002, he began to get noticed for his production style and interesting ideas, as well as his protege and artist, <a href="/wiki/Cassidy_(rapper)" title="Cassidy (rapper)">Cassidy</a>, who also started to gain recognition for his ability as well. The same year, Dean released two <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a>, "Guilty" and "Bigger Business", both of which charted on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Along with often being associated with Ruff Ryders and <a href="/wiki/Roc-A-Fella_Records" title="Roc-A-Fella Records">Roc-A-Fella Records</a>, Dean began to expand his scope to include production of artists from more mainstream labels such as <a href="/wiki/Elektra_Records" title="Elektra Records">Elektra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Bad Boy Entertainment">Bad Boy Entertainment</a>. His career largely grew from that point.
</p>
<h3><span id="2006.E2.80.9307:_Full_Surface_and_One_Man_Band_Man"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2006–07:_Full_Surface_and_One_Man_Band_Man">2006–07: Full Surface and <i>One Man Band Man</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2006–07: Full Surface and One Man Band Man">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Full_Surface_Records" title="Full Surface Records">Full Surface Records</a> and <a href="/wiki/One_Man_Band_Man" title="One Man Band Man">One Man Band Man</a></div>
<p>In February 2007, design duo <a href="/wiki/Heatherette" title="Heatherette">Heatherette</a> staged their Fall 2007 New York <a href="/wiki/Fashion_week" title="Fashion week">Fashion Week</a> <a href="/wiki/Runway_show" class="mw-redirect" title="Runway show">runway show</a>, and Dean was asked to mix the music.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In June 2007, Swizz Beatz produced and was featured on his Full Surface artist Cassidy's comeback single, "<a href="/wiki/My_Drink_n_My_2_Step" title="My Drink n My 2 Step">My Drink n My 2 Step</a>", following a murder trial and a car accident. The song proved to be a hit, reaching the <a href="/wiki/Top_40" title="Top 40">Top 40</a> of the US <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_100" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot 100">Hot 100</a> chart. On August 21, 2007, Dean released his solo debut <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" class="mw-redirect" title="Studio album">studio album</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/One_Man_Band_Man" title="One Man Band Man">One Man Band Man</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-official_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The album, preceded by the <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead singles</a> "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Me_Bitches" title="It&#39;s Me Bitches">It's Me Bitches</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Money_in_the_Bank_(Swizz_Beatz_song)" title="Money in the Bank (Swizz Beatz song)">Money in the Bank</a>", debuted at number seven on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">Billboard 200</a> and sold 45,000 copies in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-official_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 19, 2007, he launched a contest called "Share the Studio", presented by Music Video 2.0 and <a href="/wiki/The_Source_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Source (magazine)"><i>The Source</i></a> magazine. The contest was intended to be a continuation of the work from his debut album.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later that same year, Dean signed former Ruff Ryders cohorts and longtime friends, <a href="/wiki/Drag-On" title="Drag-On">Drag-On</a><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and Eve, to <a href="/wiki/Full_Surface_Records" title="Full Surface Records">Full Surface Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> He also signed legendary <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>-based hip hop group <a href="/wiki/Bone_Thugs-n-Harmony" title="Bone Thugs-n-Harmony">Bone Thugs-n-Harmony</a>, where they later released their seventh studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Strength_%26_Loyalty" title="Strength &amp; Loyalty">Strength &amp; Loyalty</a></i> in May, which Dean executive produced.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a December 2007 interview with <i>Format Magazine</i>, Dean stated that he was already working on his second studio album, at the time under the title <i>Life After the Party</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2008.E2.80.9318:_Monster_Music_Group"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008–18:_Monster_Music_Group">2008–18: Monster Music Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2008–18: Monster Music Group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, Dean began working on his second studio album. In late 2007, in an interview with <i>Format Magazine</i> he had announced the title as <i>Life After the Party</i> saying: "The opportunities that I've got from doing my album (<i>One Man Band Man</i>) are much bigger than just producing. A lot of things came from me being able to put a voice to my face. It was me just expressing myself and having the opportunity to – it was the one man band. And now I'm doing part two, which is <i>Life After the Party</i>."<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2009, Dean released a song titled "You Stay on My Mind".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On April 24, 2009, he released a promotional song for <a href="/wiki/Hennessy" title="Hennessy">Hennessy</a> Black, titled "When I Step in the Club". A music video, directed by <a href="/wiki/Hype_Williams" title="Hype Williams">Hype Williams</a>, was also released.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, Dean produced many popular singles including "<a href="/wiki/Nasty_Girl_(Ludacris_song)" title="Nasty Girl (Ludacris song)">Nasty Girl</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/Plies_(rapper)" title="Plies (rapper)">Plies</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Who%27s_Real" title="Who&#39;s Real">Who's Real</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/OJ_da_Juiceman" title="OJ da Juiceman">OJ da Juiceman</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Million_Bucks" title="Million Bucks">Million Bucks</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Maino_(rapper)" title="Maino (rapper)">Maino</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Million_Dollar_Bill" title="Million Dollar Bill">Million Dollar Bill</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>, "<a href="/wiki/I_Can_Transform_Ya" title="I Can Transform Ya">I Can Transform Ya</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown_(American_entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chris Brown (American entertainer)">Chris Brown</a> featuring Lil Wayne, and "<a href="/wiki/On_to_the_Next_One" title="On to the Next One">On to the Next One</a>" by Jay-Z.<sup id="cite_ref-umusicpub_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umusicpub-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 12, 2010, he and 81 other artists including Kanye West, Lil Wayne, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Foxx" title="Jamie Foxx">Jamie Foxx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">Will.i.am</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a>, debuted "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_World_25_for_Haiti" title="We Are the World 25 for Haiti">We Are the World 25 for Haiti</a>" during the Opening Ceremonies of the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter Olympics">Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>. Inspired by <i><a href="/wiki/GOOD_Fridays" title="GOOD Fridays">GOOD Fridays</a></i> the 2010 weekly series of free <a href="/wiki/Mp3" class="mw-redirect" title="Mp3">mp3s</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>, Swizz Beatz launched his own series titled <i>Monster Mondays</i> later that year. The first offering, "DJ Play that Beat", featured <a href="/wiki/Estelle_(musician)" title="Estelle (musician)">Estelle</a>, and was released on October 25. Other <i>Monster Monday</i> tracks feature <a href="/wiki/Rakim" title="Rakim">Rakim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pusha_T" title="Pusha T">Pusha T</a>, DMX, Busta Rhymes, <a href="/wiki/Pharrell" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharrell">Pharrell</a> and many more.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dean's second album in the works had been renamed on three occasions: initially, the album was renamed <i>King Issues</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and was later retitled <i>The Perception of Greatness</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> After initially turning to fans to help decide on an album title, Dean eventually announced in August 2010, while in a New York City recording session with <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, that the title would be <i>Haute Living</i>, as "it's the perfect phrase to state what he's all about".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In November 2010, Dean previewed the album and confirmed guest appearances from <a href="/wiki/Bono" title="Bono">Bono</a>, <a href="/wiki/Travis_Barker" title="Travis Barker">Travis Barker</a>, Kanye West, Lil Wayne, Jay-Z, <a href="/wiki/Lenny_Kravitz" title="Lenny Kravitz">Lenny Kravitz</a>, Mary J. Blige and <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a>, as well as his wife Alicia Keys.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2011, in an exclusive listening session with Rap-Up.com, Dean premiered fourteen tracks set to appear on the album, including "V.I.P. Chillin" and also several previously unheard songs, including "Dance Like a White Girl" and "Instructions".<sup id="cite_ref-rap-up1_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rap-up1-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He also premiered unfinished versions of several music videos made for the album, revealing that the Reebok-commissioned video for "International Party" cost $1.4 million to shoot,<sup id="cite_ref-rap-up1_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rap-up1-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and that the video for "You Stay on My Mind" was shot in Dubai: he also revealed that he persuaded the Sheikh to let him use the airspace for only a dollar.<sup id="cite_ref-rap-up1_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rap-up1-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Dean announced that he was planning to release the album on September 13, to coincide with his birth date.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Rather than being released under his own imprint, the album is set to be released under his legal contract with Everest Entertainment/<a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a>/<a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a>, who signed the rapper in August 2010.
</p><p>His first <a href="/wiki/53rd_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="53rd Grammy Awards">Grammy Award</a> came in 2011, awarded in the category of <a href="/wiki/Best_Rap_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Rap Performance by a Duo or Group">Best Rap Performance by a Duo or Group</a> for a track titled "<a href="/wiki/On_to_the_Next_One" title="On to the Next One">On to the Next One</a>" teaming him with Jay-Z. The first promotional single from <i>Haute Living</i> was titled "Everyday (Coolin')", features a verse from Eve, was produced by Joe Lindsay, and was released through <i>monstermondays.com</i> on March 28, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In an April 2011 interview with Paper Mag, Dean revealed that a few yet-to-be-released special collaborations would appear on the album, including one titled "Skyscrapers" featuring Kanye West and Bono: "We got this song–it's me, Bono and Kanye on this one song called 'Skyscrapers'. I recorded with Kanye in the studio and then I recorded with Bono in this actual studio right here. Mary J. Blige is on the album too; John Legend. But they're all on the album in super amazing ways. It's not like a compilation–it's a nice mixture of creativity. I had no boundaries with it; I had great partners on the album–Reebok was supporting me."<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2011, during an interview with BBC Radio 1Xtra's DJ Semtex, Swizz Beatz announced the release of his upcoming third solo album <i>Haute Living</i>, would be released on his birthday, September 13, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In July 2011, Swizz Beatz said instead of releasing all of the songs at once, he would release the tracks over an extended period of time: "Let me clarify: Haute Living is still coming, but as far as releasing all on one day, I'm not doing that no more," he said. "I want to just drop singles from <i>Haute Living</i> instead of 'I'm coming on September 13.' I'm like, 'You know what? Let me make every song an event, instead of just that one day being an event.'"<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dean and his Monster Music Group signed a joint venture with Imagem Music USA.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In a press release, the artist confirmed his excitement at his upcoming partnership with Richard Stumpf and the entire group over at Imagem Music, saying: "This partnership will enable me to further develop my group of talented producers and also introduce many new producers and writers to the world". Protégé Musicman Ty and Naki "Snagz" Levy were the first acts to sign with Monster Music Publishing,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and on May 21, 2011, he further confirmed that <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> was working on the album with him.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
In March 2012, Dean announced that he would be releasing a <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> titled <i>Limitless</i>, featuring guest appearances from DMX, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, Rick Ross, <a href="/wiki/The_LOX" class="mw-redirect" title="The LOX">The LOX</a> and <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Rocky" title="ASAP Rocky">ASAP Rocky</a>, the latter of whom is featured on the first single, "Street Knock".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On March 22, 2012, "Street Knock" featuring ASAP Rocky was premiered on "The <a href="/wiki/Angie_Martinez" title="Angie Martinez">Angie Martinez</a> Show".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In October 2012, at the 2012-2013 <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a> Season Tip-Off event at the Beacon Theatre on 73rd Street and Broadway, special guest Swizz Beatz performed a 10-minute medley of his hits, alongside the New York Knicks' City Dancers and premiered the starting line-up theme song for the upcoming season, which he produced.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On November 2, 2012, he released a new single titled "Everyday Birthday", featuring Chris Brown and <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>. Dean produced the song with Jukebox.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On August 23, 2013, he released "Hands Up", a new single featuring Lil Wayne, <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2_Chainz" title="2 Chainz">2 Chainz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On October 21, 2014, he released "Freaky", a new single featuring American rapper La'Vega.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2014, Dean was inducted into the Bronx Walk of Fame, where he received a street named in his honor, called "Swizz Beatz Street".<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2015, it was announced that Dean would host the third annual Global Spin Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, Dean and One Man Kru appeared as the only two American talents on the 6th season of popular South Korean hip hop TV show "Show Me The Money".<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.93present:_Poison_and_Verzuz"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–present:_Poison_and_Verzuz">2018–present: <i>Poison</i> and <i>Verzuz</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2018–present: Poison and Verzuz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2018, Dean released the song "It's Okayyy", ahead of the release of his then upcoming album <i><a href="/wiki/Poison_(Swizz_Beatz_album)" title="Poison (Swizz Beatz album)">Poison</a></i>. He recorded 70 songs and used 10 for the album. <i>Poison</i> features <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>, Lil Wayne, Pusha T, Nas, <a href="/wiki/Young_Thug" title="Young Thug">Young Thug</a>, The Lox, 2 Chainz, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In July 2018, Dean said he worked with Nas on the latter's follow-up to his 2018 release <i><a href="/wiki/Nasir_(album)" title="Nasir (album)">Nasir</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Dean released  "Pistol on My Side" featuring Lil Wayne from <i>Poison</i>, along with its music video, on September 14, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2020, Dean, along with <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>, launched the highly popular <i><a href="/wiki/Verzuz" title="Verzuz">Verzuz</a></i> Instagram webcast series.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In 2021, for their work on <i>Verzuz</i>, they both appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100"><i>Time</i> 100</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s annual list of the 100 most influential people in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>That same year, Dean became series music producer for the ABC TV show <i><a href="/wiki/Queens_(American_TV_series)" title="Queens (American TV series)">Queens</a></i> starring <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>, Eve, <a href="/wiki/Naturi_Naughton" title="Naturi Naughton">Naturi Naughton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nadine_Velazquez" title="Nadine Velazquez">Nadine Velazquez</a>. <i>Queens</i> premiered on October 19, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion_designer">Fashion designer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Fashion designer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2003, he became a partner involved in the popular clothing company <a href="/wiki/Kidrobot" title="Kidrobot">Kidrobot</a>, a creator and retailer of limited-edition art toys and clothing.<sup id="cite_ref-umusicpub_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umusicpub-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On Twitter in 2010, Dean revealed his new sneaker line with <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dean is an avid art collector and connoisseur actively projecting and displaying his taste via Instagram. The curated collection of favourites was first introduced at <a href="/wiki/SCOPE_Art_Show" title="SCOPE Art Show">SCOPE Art Show</a> Miami Beach and has since become known as The Dean Collection, it includes work from emerging and well established artists including <a href="/wiki/KAWS_(artist)" class="mw-redirect" title="KAWS (artist)">KAWS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Haring" title="Keith Haring">Keith Haring</a>, Cleon Peterson, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Zacharevic" title="Ernest Zacharevic">Ernest Zacharevic</a> and Erik Jones.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dean and Keys are co-chairs of the Gordon Parks Foundation, which permanently preserves the work of <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Parks" title="Gordon Parks">Gordon Parks</a>, a pioneering photographer, filmmaker, musician and activist.<sup id="cite_ref-cultured1_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cultured1-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The couple acquired what is now the largest private holding of Parks' images and what is now part of the Dean Collection, the couple's philanthropic organization and family collection of international contemporary art.<sup id="cite_ref-cultured1_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cultured1-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In the summer of 2018, Dean and Keys were featured in <i>Cultured Magazine</i> for their first joint cover, where they delved into Parks' works and the Dean Collection in more depth.<sup id="cite_ref-cultured1_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cultured1-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dean also paints in his free time. He donates the money he earns from his paintings to the Children's Cancer &amp; Blood Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_promoter">Brand promoter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Brand promoter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2010, Dean became involved in the design and launch of the Aston Martin Rapide. In 2011, Swizz Beatz became the official face of Lotus cars until CEO Dany Bahar left the company. Subsequently, Swizz Beatz returned to Aston Martin for 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2013, Dean invested in and joined the board of <a href="/wiki/Monster_Cable" title="Monster Cable">Monster</a>, and became involved in product management and marketing activities.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard_6feb2013_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_6feb2013-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forbes_7feb2013_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes_7feb2013-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Monster products that he is promoting include the <a href="/wiki/GODJ" class="mw-redirect" title="GODJ">Monster GODJ</a><sup id="cite_ref-chipchick_20131121_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chipchick_20131121-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and the Monster 24K headphones.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_20131125_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews_20131125-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dean currently sits as the Vice President - Sports Style Marketing, Design, and Brand Music Development for global footwear and apparel giant <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_Arts_Center">Performing Arts Center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Performing Arts Center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 9, 2019, it was announced that Dean and his wife, singer Alicia Keys, are planning to transform a large piece of property in Macedon, New York into a music paradise of sorts. The couple wants to make a performing arts center and recording studio out of the former Jindal Films center which includes 111 acres and 3 buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Camel_racing">Camel racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Camel racing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On October 22, 2020, Dean became the first American to win a camel race in <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> after he won his first race with his team, Kaseem abu Nasser (Saudi Bronx).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Alicia_Keys_NRJ_Music_Awards_2013.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Alicia_Keys_NRJ_Music_Awards_2013.jpg/190px-Alicia_Keys_NRJ_Music_Awards_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="268" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Alicia_Keys_NRJ_Music_Awards_2013.jpg/285px-Alicia_Keys_NRJ_Music_Awards_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Alicia_Keys_NRJ_Music_Awards_2013.jpg/380px-Alicia_Keys_NRJ_Music_Awards_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="567" data-file-height="800" /></a><figcaption>Swizz Beatz with wife <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a> in France at the <a href="/wiki/NRJ_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="NRJ Music Awards">NRJ Music Awards</a> ceremony, 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>Dean is <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> He and singer <a href="/wiki/Mashonda_Tifrere" class="mw-redirect" title="Mashonda Tifrere">Mashonda Tifrere</a> began dating in 1998. Their first pregnancy ended in a stillbirth in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, Dean's son, Nasir Dior, who is a model and a musician known as Note Marcato, with Nichole Levy was born.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Dean and Tifrere married in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Martinez_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martinez-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In December 2006, their son, Kasseem Dean Jr. was born. Dean also has a daughter Nicole, born in May 2008, with UK-based singer Jahna Sabastian, whom he met in 2007. Dean found out about his daughter a year after her birth.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Dean and Tifrere announced their break-up. According to Dean, they had been separated nine or 10 months by June 2008. Their divorce was finalized in May 2010, citing irreconcilable differences.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Martinez_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martinez-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During this time, Dean dated <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a>, whom he has known since they were teens.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> They announced they were engaged and expecting their first child in May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-expecting_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expecting-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> At the time of the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>, the couple took part of a union and had their unborn child blessed in a <a href="/wiki/Zulu_people" title="Zulu people">Zulu</a> ceremony, which took place in the <a href="/wiki/Illovo,_Gauteng" title="Illovo, Gauteng">Illovo</a> suburb of <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> They married on July 31, 2010 in a private ceremony near the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-marriage_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marriage-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Keys gave birth to their first son, Egypt Daoud Dean, in October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Egypt_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Egypt-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Their second son, Genesis Ali Dean, was born in December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Dean contributed to Tifrere's 2018 book on co-parenting with him and Keys.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, Dean was appointed the Global Ambassador for New York City Health and Hospitals Corporation (HHC).<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2014, Dean was accepted into <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Business_School" title="Harvard Business School">Harvard Business School</a>'s Owner/President Management executive program.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> In October 2017, Dean shared a video on social media, celebrating the final days leading up to his graduation: "It's been a blessing coming from the Bronx, going to Harvard. A lot of people were saying why would you go to school? It's never too late to get your education, further your education." He continued by encouraging others to seek education as well. "Knowledge is power. It don't have to be an <a href="/wiki/Ivy_league" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivy league">Ivy league</a> school. Just as long as you're doing your thing, do your thing."<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> In November 2017, Dean confirmed he had graduated from the OPM program.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2016, Dean announced that his son Egypt was a credited producer on Kendrick Lamar's compilation, <i><a href="/wiki/Untitled_Unmastered" title="Untitled Unmastered">Untitled Unmastered</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Involvement_with_Jho_Low">Involvement with Jho Low</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swizz_Beatz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Involvement with Jho Low">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2012, Dean began associating with Malaysian businessman <a href="/wiki/Jho_Low" title="Jho Low">Jho Low</a>, alleged to be the mastermind of the <a href="/wiki/1MDB_scandal" class="mw-redirect" title="1MDB scandal">1MDB scandal</a>. Dean appeared at a variety of Low's parties, and became known as one of Low's inner circle of American celebrities,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Foxx" title="Jamie Foxx">Jamie Foxx</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paris_Hilton" title="Paris Hilton">Paris Hilton</a>. Jho Low was known to give lavish gifts or cash payments to his celebrity friends<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> and Dean received an $800k payment to attend Low's lavish 31st birthday party.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Dean is also credited with helping Low navigate both the art world,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> and the music industry in the U.S.,<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> where Low acquired a number of renowned paintings and a stake in EMI music publishing, which was ultimately recovered by the U.S. Department of Justice and estimated at a value of $415 million.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
